This is the target layout for your prototype. Here's the structure:

- **Top bar** — logo, Demo/Live toggle, risk filters, live counters all in one clean strip
- **Left sidebar** — pattern filter + flagged wallets list ranked by score, floating on the globe
- **Globe** — fills the entire screen behind everything, rotating in place
- **Legend** — top right corner, semi-transparent dark card
- **Right panel** — appears when a wallet is clicked, shows network evidence and score
- **Notification** — bottom right, appears when new network is detected
- **Threat intel ticker** — bottom strip scrolling RSS feed
- **CHAINTRACE watermark** — large text behind globe exactly like the reference

This is exactly what your code should look like. Use this as the visual reference when prompting Claude Code.

[human]
how is a wallet represented here?

[assistant]
 In this mockup a wallet is represented in two ways:

---

**1. In the sidebar — as a list item**

Each wallet appears as a card with:
- A colored left border (red = high risk, amber = medium, green = low)
- A truncated wallet address in monospace font (`bc1sim3fx9k...`)
- The pattern that flagged it (`Fan-out`, `Layering` etc.)
- Its suspicion score on the right (`9.2`, `8.7` etc.)

---

**2. On the globe — as a colored dot**

Each wallet's geographic location (derived from its hash) is plotted as a small circle:
- Red glowing dot = high risk wallet
- Amber dot = medium risk
- Green dot = low risk

---

**The important distinction to understand:**

In the Elliptic dataset a "wallet" is actually a **transaction node** — not a real wallet address. The dataset anonymizes real Bitcoin addresses and represents each transaction as a node with 166 features. So what your system calls a "wallet" is technically a transaction that has been mapped to a synthetic address like `bc1sim3fx9k...`

In live mode connected to the real blockchain, each dot on the globe and each item in the sidebar would represent an actual real Bitcoin wallet address that your detection rules flagged as suspicious.

[human]
so can we make lines or edges between dots that denote a connection between transactions and how they form a network?

[assistant]
 Yes absolutely — and this is one of the most visually powerful things you can add. When an investigator clicks a dot on the globe, lines draw between all the dots in that network showing exactly how the wallets are connected and how money flowed between them.

Here's what it looks like conceptually:

- Dot A (entry) → line → Dot B (pass-through) → line → Dot C (fan-out) → lines → Dots D, E, F, G (layering) → lines → Dot H (exit/exchange)

The lines literally trace the money path across the globe.

---

**Two ways to show this:**

**On the globe itself:**
When you click a dot, curved lines appear on the globe surface connecting all wallets in that network. The lines follow the globe's curvature. Color of line = direction of flow (entry lines one color, exit lines another).

**As a separate network graph:**
A small PyVis or D3 network graph appears in the right panel showing the same network as a node-edge diagram — each wallet as a node, each transaction as a directed edge with an arrow showing money flow direction.

---

**Paste this into Claude Code:**

```
Read dashboard.py

When a dot is clicked on the globe,
draw connection lines between all wallets
in the same network.

In the Plotly globe add a new trace for 
network lines when a network is selected:

def add_network_lines(fig, network_wallets, 
                      wallet_coords):
    for i in range(len(network_wallets)):
        for j in range(i+1, len(network_wallets)):
            w1 = network_wallets[i]
            w2 = network_wallets[j]
            if w1 in wallet_coords and \
               w2 in wallet_coords:
                lat1,lon1 = wallet_coords[w1]
                lat2,lon2 = wallet_coords[w2]
                fig.add_trace(go.Scattergeo(
                    lat=[lat1, lat2],
                    lon=[lon1, lon2],
                    mode='lines',
                    line=dict(
                        width=1,
                        color='rgba(248,113,113,0.5)'
                    ),
                    showlegend=False,
                    hoverinfo='skip'
                ))
    return fig

Store selected network in session state
when a globe dot is clicked.

Also highlight the selected network wallets
as larger brighter dots on top of existing dots:

fig.add_trace(go.Scattergeo(
    lat=selected_lats,
    lon=selected_lons,
    mode='markers',
    marker=dict(
        size=16,
        color='#f87171',
        opacity=1.0,
        line=dict(width=2, color='#ffffff')
    ),
    showlegend=False,
    hoverinfo='skip'
))

Run: streamlit run dashboard.py
```

why is the sidebar with flagged wallet list required if ultimately wewant to detect networks?

[assistant]
 Great question. You're right to challenge it.

---

**The honest answer:**

If your end goal is network detection, the sidebar should show **networks** not individual wallets.

An investigator doesn't care about wallet `bc1sim3fx9k` in isolation. They care about **Network #014 — 47 wallets — $2.4M — Fan-out pattern — Score 9.2**. That's the actionable intelligence.

---

**What the sidebar should actually show:**

Instead of a list of flagged wallets, show a list of detected networks:

Fan-out + Layering · High risk

Network #007
23 wallets · $1.1M · Score 8.7
Mixer hub · High risk
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

Network #021
12 wallets · $0.6M · Score 7.3
Pass-through chain · High risk
```

Clicking a network:
- Highlights all its dots on the globe
- Draws the connection lines between them
- Loads the full network profile in the right panel

---

**The individual wallet list still has ONE use:**

When an investigator has a specific wallet address from a tip or a SAR report and wants to look it up directly — they need a search bar for that. But a ranked list of every individual flagged wallet is noise when what you really want is a ranked list of criminal networks.

[human]
ultimately what would an investigator need as output to work with for further investigation? name them

[assistant]
 Here's what an investigator actually needs as output:

---

**1. Network Evidence Report (PDF)**
A formal document they can submit as evidence or share with other agencies containing:
- Network ID, detection timestamp
- All wallet addresses in the network
- How each wallet was flagged and why
- The three-signal confidence breakdown
- Total value moved
- Fund flow path from entry to exit
- OFAC matches if any

---

**2. Transaction Trail**
A chronological list of every transaction in the network showing:
- From wallet → To wallet
- Amount
- Timestamp
- Which detection rule it triggered

This is the chain of evidence that proves money moved from A to B to C.

---

**3. Fund Flow Visualization (exportable)**
The network graph showing entry points, layering wallets, and exit points as a static image they can include in court submissions or agency reports.

---

**4. Wallet Address List (CSV)**
A simple flat file of all flagged wallet addresses so they can:
- Submit to exchanges for KYC lookup
- Cross-reference with other intelligence databases
- Share with international FIU partners

---

**5. SAR (Suspicious Activity Report) Draft**
A pre-filled template matching the official SAR format used by FinCEN or their national equivalent, populated with the network data so the investigator just reviews and submits rather than writing from scratch.

---

**6. OSINT Package**
For each wallet address, a summary of what open source intelligence exists — known exchange associations, darknet market links, prior flags in public databases.

---

**For your prototype the most realistic ones to implement are 1, 2, 3, and 4** — the PDF report, transaction trail, exportable graph, and CSV. These are what judges will recognize as genuinely useful and are buildable in your timeframe.

[human]
does claude code work better whrn given one prompt at a time or multiple together

[assistant]
 **One focused prompt at a time** works better — here's why:

---

**When you give multiple changes together:**
- Claude Code has to hold all changes in context simultaneously
- It sometimes fixes 3 out of 5 things and misses the others
- If one change causes an error it can break the others too
- Harder to know which change caused a new problem

---

**When you give one change at a time:**
- Claude Code focuses entirely on that one thing
- You can verify it worked before moving on
- If something breaks you know exactly which change caused it
- Each change gets tested independently

---

**Best workflow for your remaining fixes:**

Do them in this order, one at a time:

1. Remove "Select Net" buttons → verify → screenshot
2. Fix scores showing 2.0 → verify → screenshot
3. Move legends off globe → verify → screenshot
4. Fix globe colors → verify → screenshot

Each prompt should be under 10 lines. Short and specific. This saves tokens and gets better results.

[assistant]
 The scoring is fixed. Here's what Claude Code found and corrected:

- Fan-out threshold was too high (10) for the 3000-row demo subset — lowered to 5
- High risk patterns were only scoring +3 which landed at amber, not high — now +6 so they correctly hit the high threshold
- Layering chain required 5 hops — rarely achievable in a small dataset — lowered to 4
- Mixer hub required 6 in + 6 out — lowered to 4 in + 4 out

**Result:** Globe should now show red dots (3 high risk) and amber dots (32 medium risk) instead of all green.

when i click on a dot on the globe, all the otehr dots, be it any color fluctuate between appearing and disappearing

[assistant]
 Paste this into Claude Code:

```
Read dashboard.py

When a dot is clicked on the globe,
all other dots flicker and disappear.

This is caused by st.rerun() being 
called on click which re-renders the 
entire Plotly chart from scratch.

Fix by using uirevision to preserve 
globe state between reruns:

In fig.update_layout() add:
uirevision='globe'

This tells Plotly to preserve the 
existing rendering and only update 
what changed — stopping the flicker.

Also make sure when a network is 
selected, ALL dots still render 
as one trace, and the selected 
network dots render as a second 
trace on top — not replacing the first.

So globe always has:
Trace 1: all dots (always visible)
Trace 2: selected network dots highlighted
Trace 3: connection lines for selected network

Never remove trace 1 when a network is selected.

Run: streamlit run dashboard.py
```

[human]
Fix 1 — uirevision='globe' (fig.update_layout):                                                                                                                                                               
  Plotly uses this as a stable key to decide whether to re-initialize the chart or just diff-update it. With the same uirevision across reruns, Plotly preserves the current camera rotation, zoom, and pan —   
  only updating the data that changed. Without it, every st.rerun() triggers a full chart teardown and rebuild, causing the visible flicker.                                                                    
                                                                                                                                                                                                                
  Fix 2 — Trace 1 always contains all dots:                                                                                                                                                                     
  Previously: selected network dots were removed from trace 1 and placed only in trace 2 — so trace 1 shrank on selection and flickered as dots disappeared then reappeared. Now every dot is always appended to
   trace 1 (original color/size), and selected network dots are additionally appended to trace 2 as a highlighted overlay (larger size, white glow border). Trace 1 never loses points between reruns.          
                                          
  Trace order is now always:                                                                                                                                                                                    
  1. Connection lines (hub-and-spoke for selected network)
  2. City labels                                                                                                                                                                                                
  3. Trace 1: all dots (always full set)  
  4. Trace 2: selected network dots overlaid with white glow (only when a network is selected)

[human]
1. Detection cache (_fiu_det_cache in session state)                                                                                                                                                          
  The key insight: pdet.run_detection() and pdet.cluster_networks() were re-running on every rerun, including when you just click a network card. They're now cached by (step, live_mode, len(tx),              
  len(cio_clusters)). A network-selection click doesn't change any of those — so it hits the cache and skips the expensive graph traversal entirely. This alone cuts the 6-7s to <1s.                           
                                                                                                                                                                                                                
  2. Wallet coords cache (wallet_coords in session state)                                                                                                                                                       
  _wcoords() is MD5 — cheap but called 150+ times per render. Now computed once per wallet and reused.                                                                                                        
                                                                                                                                                                                                                
  3. Stable 4-trace figure                                                                                                                                                                                      
  Traces are now always exactly: 0=lines, 1=city labels, 2=dots, 3=overlay — no conditional add_trace. This prevents uirevision from breaking when trace count changes.

  After the chart renders, a components.html script attaches a plotly_click handler to the parent window's Plotly chart. When a dot is clicked, JS immediately calls Plotly.restyle(gd, {lat, lon,              
  'line.color'}, [0]) on trace 0 — lines appear before the Python rerun even starts. The Python rerun (now fast via the cache) then catches up to update the right panel.

[assistant]
 Paste this into Claude Code:

```
Read dashboard.py

Two globe rotation fixes:

1. SMOOTH ROTATION OR STOP:
Current rotation is jerky because 
st.rerun() drives it in 2 second gaps.

Remove the Python-driven rotation entirely.

Instead drive rotation purely in JavaScript
inside the HTML component using 
requestAnimationFrame:

let autoRotate = true;
let currentLon = 0;

function rotate() {
    if (autoRotate) {
        currentLon += 0.05;
        Plotly.relayout('globe-plot', {
            'geo.projection.rotation.lon': currentLon
        });
    }
    requestAnimationFrame(rotate);
}
requestAnimationFrame(rotate);

This runs at 60fps in the browser —
completely smooth, no gaps.

0.05 degrees per frame = very slow 
earthlike rotation.

2. PAUSE ROTATION WHEN USER INTERACTS:
When user drags the globe stop rotating:

document.getElementById('globe-plot')
    .on('plotly_relayout', function(e) {
        if (e['geo.projection.rotation.lon'] 
            !== undefined) {
            autoRotate = false;
        }
    });

Add a double-click to resume rotation:
document.getElementById('globe-plot')
    .on('plotly_doubleclick', function() {
        autoRotate = true;
    });

Also add a small hint text below globe:
"Double-click globe to resume rotation"

Remove all Python-side rotation code:
- Remove time.time() rotation calculation
- Remove globe_lon from session state
- Remove any st.rerun() called for rotation

Run: streamlit run dashboard.py
```

[human]
Root cause: every 3s the autorefresh advanced current_step → detection cache invalidated → nets recomputed with new IDs → selected_network (stored as int 1) no longer matched any key in the new nets →      
  _net_detail = None → panel blank.                                                                                                                                                                             
                                                                                                                                                                                                                
  Fixes applied:                                                                                                                                                                                                
  1. _sel_net_id — new session state key holds the int network ID for all lookup logic. selected_network is now exclusively the full detail dict.                                                               
  2. auto_advance = False — set on sidebar click, globe click, and wallet selection. The autorefresh tick fires but the current_step only advances if auto_advance is True.                                     
  3. Dict persisted after build — after _net_detail is constructed each rerun, st.session_state.selected_network = _net_detail saves it. Right panel reads st.session_state.get('selected_network') — the dict
  is there even if something transiently returns None.
